Extending Temporality to All Creation
Nasafi enumerates entities whose temporality follows from the previous proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi extends the proof of temporality from accidents and substances to encompass all other created entities.

Core Idea
One proof establishes the temporality of everything created.

This passage shows the sweeping conclusion of the kalam argument for the temporality of the universe. Having proven that accidents and substances are temporally originated, Imam Nasafi now applies that same logic to natures, elements, celestial bodies, time, and void. This demonstrates the comprehensive nature of the proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the conditional structure: 'If it is established... then...'
2
Identify the entities listed
The passage lists several categories: natures, hyle, elements (as called by materialists), celestial spheres with stars, sun, moon, time, and void. Identify each one in the Arabic.
These are all things that some philosophers considered eternal.
3
Understand the logical link
Ask yourself why the temporality of all these follows from the temporality of accidents and substances. The commentary explains that they all fall under the previous proof.
The author does not repeat the proof here; he refers back to it.
4
Reflect on the scope
Consider the implication: if time and void are also temporal, then nothing besides Allah is eternal. This is a key doctrine of Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ثبت بما بينا حدوث الأعراض والجواهر كلها ثبت حدوث الطبائع والهيولى وجميع ما تسميه الدهرية والطبيعيون عناصر وإسطقسات وحدوث الأفلاك بما فيها من البروج والكواكب والشمس والقمر وحدوث الزمان والخلاء إذ ذاك كله داخل تحت ما أقمنا الدلالة على حدوثه. والله الموفق.
And if it is established by what we have shown the temporality of all accidents and substances, then the temporality of natures and hyle and all that the materialists and naturalists call elements and elements, and the temporality of the celestial spheres with what they contain of zodiacal signs, planets, sun, moon, and the temporality of time and void is established, because all of that falls under what we have established of proof of its temporality. And Allah is the Granter of success.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage states that once the temporality (creation in time) of all accidents and substances has been established, it necessarily follows that everything else is also temporal. This includes the natures (طبائع), the prime matter (هيولى), all elements referred to by materialists and naturalists, the celestial spheres with their stars, the sun and moon, and even time and void. All these are encompassed by the previous proof. The author ends with a prayer for divine success.

Key Terms
أعراض
جواهر
حدوث
طبائع
هيولى
أفلاك
زمان
خلاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That only accidents and substances are temporal, but elements, celestial spheres, time, and void are eternal.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that these are all temporal because they fall under the same proof as accidents and substances.

Checkpoint
What does the proof of temporality of accidents and substances imply according to this passage?
A) Only accidents are temporal
B) Only substances are temporal
C) Everything including natures, spheres, time, and void is temporal
D) Only the material world is temporal

Key Takeaway
The proof for the temporality of accidents and substances establishes the temporality of all created entities, including natures, celestial spheres, time, and void.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If time itself is a created temporal entity, then every moment of your life is a gift from Allah that could cease at any instant. How would your plans for next week change if you truly believed that time could end before then? What is one thing you would do today if you knew you might not have tomorrow?
?
The celestial spheres, sun, moon, and stars are all temporal and will pass away. Yet you often live as if the sun will always rise. How would your waking thought change if you reminded yourself each morning: 'This day could be the last; the sun may not rise tomorrow'? Write one concrete change you will make in your morning routine to internalize this temporality.

Refuting the Dahriyya's Argument for an Eternal World
Nasafi refutes the Dahriyya's division argument for an eternal world with no creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi refutes the Dahriyya's argument that the world must be eternal because the mechanism of creation is inconceivable, using a clear proof and an analogy about crossing a river.

Core Idea
Ignorance of how creation happened does not disprove that it happened.

The Dahriyya (materialists) argued that the world must be eternal because if it were created, the process of creation would have to be either eternal or originated, both of which they deemed impossible. Nasafi responds decisively: the world's origination has already been established by undeniable proof. He then uses a striking analogy to show that inability to imagine the 'how' does not negate the 'that'.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Dahriyya's division argument
Read the first part of the passage where Nasafi presents their reasoning: the world cannot be originated because origination leads to absurdities.
Notice how they divide possibilities to claim all are invalid.
2
Grasp Nasafi's core response
Notice that Nasafi first asserts the proof for origination is certain, then argues that ignorance of the mode does not invalidate the proof.
The key phrase is 'الجهل بكيفية طريق شيء ما لا يوجب انتفاؤه'.
3
Analyze the river analogy
Read the analogy carefully. How does it illustrate the logical fallacy of denying a proven fact due to ignorance of its mechanism?
The analogy shows that direct evidence outweighs inability to explain the method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما القائلون منهم بأنه قديم ولا صانع له وتعلقهم أنه لو كان محدثا أما أن كان بإحداث أو لا بإحداث والإحداث إما قديم وإما حادث وكل الأقسام باطل. فنقول لهم والله الموفق : إن حدوث العالم بجميع أقسامه قد ثبت بدليل لا شبهة فيه، فبعد ذلك ما تعلقتم به من الكلام فيه بيان جهلكم بكيفية طريق الحدوث والجهل بكيفية طريق شيء ما لا يوجب انتفاؤه عند قيام الدليل على ثبوته، ألا ترى أن من كان على شط نهر عظيم هائل تقرر في ظنه أن لا يتصور للعبور عنه بوجه من الوجوه، وقد رأى إنسانا وراء النهر، ثم رأى ذلك الرجل بعد ذلك في هذا الجانب من النهر لم يبق للرائي شك في أنه غير النهر لا محالة وإن كان لا يعلم كيفية طريق عبوره، ولو أنكر عبوره مع معاينته إياه في هذا الجانب من النهر لما كان يعد مكابرا معاندا فكذا هذا.
As for those among them who say that it (the world) is eternal and has no maker, and their argument is that if it were originated, then either by an origination or without an origination, and the origination is either eternal or originated, and all the divisions are invalid. We say to them, and God is the grantor of success: The temporal origination of the world in all its divisions has been established by a proof in which there is no doubt. After that, what you have attached to it of discourse is an expression of your ignorance of the mode of the way of origination, and ignorance of the mode of a thing does not necessitate its negation when proof for its existence stands. Do you not see that if someone is on the bank of a great, tremendous river, and it is established in his mind that passage across it is inconceivable in any way, and then he sees a man on the other side of the river, and then sees that same man afterwards on this side of the river, no doubt remains for the observer that he indeed crossed the river, even if he does not know the mode of his crossing? And if he denied his crossing despite witnessing him on this side of the river, he would be considered a stubborn contester. So likewise this.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage refutes the argument of the Dahriyya (materialists) who claim the world is eternal and has no creator. Their argument is a division: if the world were originated, it must be either by an origination (i.e., a creative act) or without an origination; and if by an origination, that origination must be either eternal or originated. They claim all possibilities are invalid, thus the world must be eternal. Nasafi responds by first stating that the origination of the world has been proven by a clear proof. Then he argues that their objection is based on ignorance of the mode of origination, and ignorance of the mode does not negate the fact when proof exists. He gives an analogy: a man sees another on the opposite bank of a river he thinks impossible to cross, but later sees him on the same side. He cannot deny the crossing occurred even if he does not know how. Similarly, the origination of the world is proven, and their inability to conceive the mode does not invalidate it.

Key Terms
قديم
محدث
إحداث
حدوث
بدليل
كيفية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if we cannot explain how God created the world, then creation itself is doubtful.
Correction: Nasafi teaches that the fact of creation is established by proof, and our inability to describe the mechanism does not undermine that proof, just as we accept a man crossed a river even if we don't know how.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the status of the proof for the world's origination?
A) It is merely probable.
B) It is established by a proof with no doubt.
C) It depends on knowing the mode.
D) It is rejected by the Dahriyya.

Key Takeaway
The proof of creation stands on its own; ignorance of how it happened does not invalidate it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter something in your faith that you cannot fully explain—like the precise mechanism of creation—does your lack of understanding ever cause you to doubt? What would it take for you to trust the clear evidence you already have, even without knowing the 'how'?
?
The river analogy shows that a person can be certain of a crossing despite not seeing how it happened. In your own life, what undeniable signs of God's existence have you witnessed? Are you using your limited understanding as an excuse to avoid submitting to the truth?
?
If you are honest, do you sometimes find yourself demanding that God explain every detail before you believe? How can you cultivate the humility to accept what has been proven, even when the mechanism remains hidden?

The Dilemma of Ihdath: Attribute or Other
Nasafi presents the three possible meanings of ihdath and refutes the first two.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila position on the origination of the world leads to either affirming a second eternal being or an infinite regress.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila must choose: either ihdath is God's attribute, or something else — both are self-defeating.

Nasafi begins his refutation by setting up a logical dilemma for the Mu'tazila. He asks them to define what they mean by 'ihdath' (bringing into existence). Their answer forces them into contradiction with their own principles. In this lesson, we walk through the first two possibilities and their devastating consequences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once. Notice how Nasafi phrases the three options as a direct question to the Mu'tazila.
2
Identify the first two options
Look for the first two possibilities: ihdath as God's attribute, and ihdath as something other than God. Note the consequences for each.
3
Understand the infinite regress
If ihdath is originated, it needs another ihdath, leading to an infinite chain. Ask yourself why this is unacceptable in kalam.
Infinite regress is impossible because it would never end.
4
Connect to the core idea
Reflect on how both options contradict Mu'tazila principles: attributing ihdath to God affirms an attribute, while making it other-than-God leads to a second eternal or infinite regress.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجوهر والجسم، فأما الموجود فيستحيل اتصافه في أول أحوال وجوده بأنه متحرك أو ساكن أو ماش أو قاعد أو أكل أو شارب، فيستحيل أيضا اتصافه بها في حالة العدم، ثم من زعم منهم أن الأحداث ليس بصفة للباري عز وجل بل عين المحدث، فيقال : ما معنى قولكم بأن العالم محدث، أكان محدثا بأحداث هو صفة الله تعالى قائمة به أو بإحداث هو عين المحدث أو بإحداث هو غير المحدث وليس بصفة الله تعالى قائمة به ؟ فإن قالوا : حدث بإحداث هو صفة الله تعالى، قيل هذا ترك منكم مذهبكم وإن زعموا أنه حدث بإحداث هو غير الله تعالى، قيل أقديم هو أم محدث؟ فإن قالوا هو قديم فقد تركوا مذهبهم وإن قالوا هو محدث، قيل: إن حدث أيضا بإحداث آخر أم لا بإحداث؟ فإن قالوا: لا بإحداث فقد أحالوا وعطلوا الصانع حيث جوزوا حدوث حادث لا بإحداث، وإن قالوا حدث بإحداث آخر سئلوا عن الإحداث الثاني والثالث فيتسلسل إلى غير نهاية، وفيه تعليق حدوث العالم بما يستحيل ثبوته، وإن قالوا حدث بإحداث هو ذاته، فقد جعلوا ذات العالم في العدم إحداثا وهو في الأزل كان ذاتا وكان جوهرا وأعراض وأجساما فكانت محدثة في الأزل، والموجود في الأزل لن يكون محدثا بل يكون قديما ، فإذا كان العالم قديما موجودا في الأزل، فاعترضوا على هذا وزعموا أن معنى قولنا: إن العالم حدث أي حصل على حالة لم يكن عليها قبل هذه الحالة ، معنى راجع إلى ذات العالم أم هي معنى وراء ذات العالم فبأي الجواب أجابوا فقد أبطلنا، وتبين أنه حصل بهذا الاعتراض لاغيا هاذيا ثم يقال لهم إذا كان الموجود موجودا لذاته لا لمعنى، وكذا الشيء شيئا لذاته لا لمعنى، أكان المعدوم ذاتا؟ فإن قالوا: لا، قيل: لم كان شيئا والشيء شيء لذاته، وكذا العرض والجوهر، وإن قالوا: كان المعدوم ذاتا قيل لم يكن موجودا، والذات الذي لأجله يتصف بالوجود قائم بظهر بهذا أي قولهم نتيجة قول الدهرية بل هو عين ذلك بل هو شر من قول أصحاب الهيولى بدرجات فإن أولئك ما أثبتوا في الأزل إلا الهيولى وهو شيء متحد الذات عندهم لا كمية له ولا كيفية وليس بجوهر ولا عرض، وهؤلاء أثبتوا جميع أجزاء العالم في الأزل، ثم من قال منهم أن المعدوم جسم في حالة العدم وجوهر أيضا قيل له الجسم هو المتركب، والجوهر ما قام به الأعراض، أكان التركب قائما بالجسم في الأزل والعرض بالجوهر؟ فإن قال: نعم، فقد جعل العرض قائما بالمعدوم وهو محال، وإن قال: لا، فقد أثبت جسما لا تركيب له وجوهرا لم يقم به العرض، وفيه إبطال كون الجسم متركبا، والجوهر حاملا للأعراض، وفيه تصحيح قول المجسمة والنصارى، ولقد صدق من قال : إن المعتزلة مخانيث الدهرية، ووراء هذا للمعتزلة أصول فاسدة أبطلوا بها على أنفسهم إثبات حدوث العالم. وكذا الكرامية وغيرهم من أهل البدع، إلا أنا تركنا ذكرها مخافة التطويل ونشير إلى بعض ذلك إذا انتهينا إلى الكلام معهم في إبطال مذاهبهم، ولأهل الحق طرق كثيرة في إثبات حدوث العالم، أعرضنا عن ذكرها تحرزا عن التطويل وعلما منا بكافية هذه الطريقة. وبالوقوف على هذه الجملة عرف بطلان قول كل من يدعي قدم شيء ما سوى الله
And the substance and the body. As for the existent, it is impossible for it to be described in the first state of its existence as moving or stationary or walking or sitting or eating or drinking, and it is also impossible for it to be described with these in the state of non-existence. Then whoever among them claims that events [originations] are not an attribute of the Creator, glory be to Him, but are identical to the originated thing, it is said: What is the meaning of your statement that the world is originated? Was it originated by an originating (ihdath) that is an attribute of God, exalted, subsisting in Him, or by an originating that is identical to the originated, or by an originating that is other than the originated and not an attribute of God, exalted, subsisting in Him? If they say: It originated by an originating that is an attribute of God, it is said: This is an abandonment of your school. If they claim that it originated by an originating that is other than God, it is said: Is that originating eternal or originated? If they say it is eternal, they have abandoned their school; if they say it is originated, it is said: Did it also originate by another originating or not by an originating? If they say: Not by an originating, they have committed an absurdity and negated the Maker, for they allowed the occurrence of an originated event without an originating. If they say it originated by another originating, they are asked about the second and third originating, and so on ad infinitum, and in this is the suspension of the origination of the world upon something whose establishment is impossible. And if they say it originated by an originating that is its essence, then they have made the essence of the world in non-existence an originating, while in pre-eternity it was an essence and was substance, accidents, and bodies, so they were originated in pre-eternity. And that which exists in pre-eternity cannot be originated but is eternal. So if the world is eternal, existing in pre-eternity, then they object to this and claim that the meaning of our statement 'the world originated' is that it came to be in a state it was not in before this state. Is this meaning referable to the essence of the world or is it a meaning beyond the essence of the world? Whichever answer they give, we have refuted it. And it becomes clear that this objection is vain and absurd. Then it is said to them: If the existent exists by itself and not by a meaning, and likewise a thing is a thing by itself and not by a meaning, was the non-existent an essence? If they say no, it is said: Why was it a thing, while a thing is a thing by itself? Likewise the accident and the substance. And if they say the non-existent was an essence, it is said: Then it was not existent. And the essence by which it is described with existence subsists in...? By this their statement is the result of the statement of the Dahriyya, rather it is the same, rather it is worse than the statement of the proponents of hylé by degrees. For those only posited in pre-eternity the hylé, which is a thing unified in essence according to them, having no quantity nor quality, and is neither substance nor accident. And these [Mu'tazila] posited all parts of the world in pre-eternity. Then if one of them says that the non-existent is a body in the state of non-existence and also a substance, it is said to him: The body is that which is composed, and the substance is that in which accidents subsist. Was composition subsisting in the body in pre-eternity, and accident in the substance? If he says yes, he has made an accident subsist in the non-existent, which is impossible. If he says no, he has posited a body without composition and a substance without accident subsisting in it, which invalidates the definition of body as composed and substance as bearer of accidents, and this validates the statement of the anthropomorphists and the Christians. And truthful is he who said: The Mu'tazila are the effeminate of the Dahriyya. And besides this, the Mu'tazila have corrupt principles by which they have themselves refuted the proof of the origination of the world. Likewise the Karramiyya and other people of innovation, except that we have omitted mentioning them for fear of prolixity, and we will indicate some of that when we come to the discussion with them in refuting their schools. The people of truth have many ways of proving the origination of the world; we have refrained from mentioning them to avoid prolixity and because we consider this method sufficient. And by understanding this summary, the falsehood of the statement of everyone who claims the eternity of anything other than God is known.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila position on how the world becomes originated (hadith). Nasafi begins by noting that an existent cannot be described with accidents like motion, rest, etc., in its first moment of existence, nor in non-existence. Then he addresses the Mu'tazila claim that events (ahdath) are not an attribute of God but identical to the originated thing. He poses a dilemma: the word 'ihdath' (bringing into existence) — is it an attribute of God, or the originated itself, or something else? If it is an attribute of God, the Mu'tazila have abandoned their school (since they deny attributes). If it is something other than God, is it eternal or originated? If eternal, they admit a second eternal. If originated, they fall into infinite regress (tasalsul) because each ihdath would need another ihdath. If they say it is the essence itself, then the world's essence was in non-existence as an ihdath, implying that in pre-eternity the world's essence (substances, accidents, bodies) was already present, making it eternal — contradicting its origination. Then Nasafi refutes their redefinition of 'originated' as 'coming to be in a state it was not in before'. He argues that this meaning either refers to the essence or is additional; both are shown to be impossible. He then shifts to another argument: existence and thingness are intrinsic, not by a meaning. He asks whether the non-existent was an essence (dhat). If they say no, then how could it be a thing? If yes, then it was not existent. Their position ultimately aligns with the Dahriyya (materialists) or is even worse. Nasafi then refutes the claim that the non-existent is a body or substance, showing that it would require composition or accidents in non-existence, which is absurd. He concludes by noting that the Mu'tazila have many other corrupt principles, and the people of truth have sufficient proofs for the origination of the world, so this summary suffices to refute all claims of eternal entities besides God.

Key Terms
محدث
إحداث
ذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu'tazila position on origination is coherent and avoids attributes.
Correction: Nasafi shows that their denial of attributes forces them into either admitting a second eternal being or an infinite regress, both of which are worse.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what happens if the Mu'tazila say that ihdath is something other than God and it is originated?
A) They have abandoned their school.
B) They admit a second eternal being.
C) They face an infinite regress.
D) They affirm an attribute of God.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila are caught in a dilemma: if ihdath is God's attribute, they contradict themselves; if it is something else, they fall into infinite regress or polytheism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Nasafi’s refutation exposes hidden contradictions in the Mu'tazila's position. Have you ever held a belief about Allah that, when examined closely, led to a logical inconsistency? What did you do about it—ignore it or seek clarity from the Quran and Sunnah?
?
The argument shows that denying an attribute of Allah leads to absurd consequences like infinite regress or shirk. Are there any attributes of Allah you find difficult to accept or tend to rationalize away? How will you strengthen your belief in them starting today?
?
Infinite regress is impossible, meaning everything must have a beginning caused by the Eternal. Does this truth change how you view your own actions and their ultimate reliance on Allah? How will you live in greater awareness of His constant role as the Creator?

The Essence Option and Redefinition Refuted
Nasafi refutes the third option and the Mu'tazila redefinition of origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why claiming that ihdath is identical to the essence of the world leads to the absurdity of the world being eternal, and why the Mu'tazila redefinition of 'originated' as a change of state is incoherent.

Core Idea
If ihdath is the world's essence, the world is eternal; if 'originated' means change of state, it cannot explain coming from non-existence.

Nasafi now tackles the third possibility: that ihdath is identical to the essence of the world. He shows that this implies the world's essence existed in pre-eternity, making it eternal. Then he addresses the Mu'tazila attempt to redefine 'originated' as a mere change of state, and demonstrates that this too fails.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic for the third option and the subsequent objection. Notice how Nasafi forces the Mu'tazila into a contradiction: if ihdath is the essence, the world's components were present in pre-eternity.
2
Understand the essence argument
If the world's essence is ihdath, then in pre-eternity, the world's substance and accidents were already there, making the world eternal. This contradicts the claim of origination.
3
Analyze the redefinition
The Mu'tazila then claim 'originated' means coming to be in a state not previously had. Nasafi asks whether this meaning is the essence or additional. Either way, it is shown impossible.
4
See the conclusion
Nasafi declares that this objection is vain and absurd (laghiyan hadhiyan), demonstrating the failure of the Mu'tazila position.

بإحداث هو صفة الله تعالى، قيل هذا ترك منكم مذهبكم وإن زعموا أنه حدث بإحداث هو غير الله تعالى، قيل أقديم هو أم محدث؟ فإن قالوا هو قديم فقد تركوا مذهبهم وإن قالوا هو محدث، قيل: إن حدث أيضا بإحداث آخر أم لا بإحداث؟ فإن قالوا: لا بإحداث فقد أحالوا وعطلوا الصانع حيث جوزوا حدوث حادث لا بإحداث، وإن قالوا حدث بإحداث آخر سئلوا عن الإحداث الثاني والثالث فيتسلسل إلى غير نهاية، وفيه تعليق حدوث العالم بما يستحيل ثبوته، وإن قالوا حدث بإحداث هو ذاته، فقد جعلوا ذات العالم في العدم إحداثا وهو في الأزل كان ذاتا وكان جوهرا وأعراض وأجساما فكانت محدثة في الأزل، والموجود في الأزل لن يكون محدثا بل يكون قديما ، فإذا كان العالم قديما موجودا في الأزل، فاعترضوا على هذا وزعموا أن معنى قولنا: إن العالم حدث أي حصل على حالة لم يكن عليها قبل هذه الحالة ، معنى راجع إلى ذات العالم أم هي معنى وراء ذات العالم فبأي الجواب أجابوا فقد أبطلنا، وتبين أنه حصل بهذا الاعتراض لاغيا هاذيا ثم يقال لهم إذا كان الموجود موجودا لذاته لا لمعنى، وكذا الشيء شيئا لذاته لا لمعنى، أكان المعدوم ذاتا؟ فإن قالوا: لا، قيل: لم كان شيئا والشيء شيء لذاته، وكذا العرض والجوهر، وإن قالوا: كان المعدوم ذاتا قيل لم يكن موجودا، والذات الذي لأجله يتصف بالوجود قائم بظهر بهذا أي قولهم نتيجة قول الدهرية بل هو عين ذلك بل هو شر من قول أصحاب الهيولى بدرجات فإن أولئك ما أثبتوا في الأزل إلا الهيولى وهو شيء متحد الذات عندهم لا كمية له ولا كيفية وليس بجوهر ولا عرض، وهؤلاء أثبتوا جميع أجزاء العالم في الأزل، ثم من قال منهم أن المعدوم جسم في حالة العدم وجوهر أيضا قيل له الجسم هو المتركب، والجوهر ما قام به الأعراض، أكان التركب قائما بالجسم في الأزل والعرض بالجوهر؟ فإن قال: نعم، فقد جعل العرض قائما بالمعدوم وهو محال، وإن قال: لا، فقد أثبت جسما لا تركيب له وجوهرا لم يقم به العرض، وفيه إبطال كون الجسم متركبا، والجوهر حاملا للأعراض، وفيه تصحيح قول المجسمة والنصارى، ولقد صدق من قال : إن المعتزلة مخانيث الدهرية، ووراء هذا للمعتزلة أصول فاسدة أبطلوا بها على أنفسهم إثبات حدوث العالم. وكذا الكرامية وغيرهم من أهل البدع، إلا أنا تركنا ذكرها مخافة التطويل ونشير إلى بعض ذلك إذا انتهينا إلى الكلام معهم في إبطال مذاهبهم، ولأهل الحق طرق كثيرة في إثبات حدوث العالم، أعرضنا عن ذكرها تحرزا عن التطويل وعلما منا بكافية هذه الطريقة. وبالوقوف على هذه الجملة عرف بطلان قول كل من يدعي قدم شيء ما سوى الله
And the substance and the body. As for the existent, it is impossible for it to be described in the first state of its existence as moving or stationary or walking or sitting or eating or drinking, and it is also impossible for it to be described with these in the state of non-existence. Then whoever among them claims that events [originations] are not an attribute of the Creator, glory be to Him, but are identical to the originated thing, it is said: What is the meaning of your statement that the world is originated? Was it originated by an originating (ihdath) that is an attribute of God, exalted, subsisting in Him, or by an originating that is identical to the originated, or by an originating that is other than the originated and not an attribute of God, exalted, subsisting in Him? If they say: It originated by an originating that is an attribute of God, it is said: This is an abandonment of your school. If they claim that it originated by an originating that is other than God, it is said: Is that originating eternal or originated? If they say it is eternal, they have abandoned their school; if they say it is originated, it is said: Did it also originate by another originating or not by an originating? If they say: Not by an originating, they have committed an absurdity and negated the Maker, for they allowed the occurrence of an originated event without an originating. If they say it originated by another originating, they are asked about the second and third originating, and so on ad infinitum, and in this is the suspension of the origination of the world upon something whose establishment is impossible. And if they say it originated by an originating that is its essence, then they have made the essence of the world in non-existence an originating, while in pre-eternity it was an essence and was substance, accidents, and bodies, so they were originated in pre-eternity. And that which exists in pre-eternity cannot be originated but is eternal. So if the world is eternal, existing in pre-eternity, then they object to this and claim that the meaning of our statement 'the world originated' is that it came to be in a state it was not in before this state. Is this meaning referable to the essence of the world or is it a meaning beyond the essence of the world? Whichever answer they give, we have refuted it. And it becomes clear that this objection is vain and absurd. Then it is said to them: If the existent exists by itself and not by a meaning, and likewise a thing is a thing by itself and not by a meaning, was the non-existent an essence? If they say no, it is said: Why was it a thing, while a thing is a thing by itself? Likewise the accident and the substance. And if they say the non-existent was an essence, it is said: Then it was not existent. And the essence by which it is described with existence subsists in...? By this their statement is the result of the statement of the Dahriyya, rather it is the same, rather it is worse than the statement of the proponents of hylé by degrees. For those only posited in pre-eternity the hylé, which is a thing unified in essence according to them, having no quantity nor quality, and is neither substance nor accident. And these [Mu'tazila] posited all parts of the world in pre-eternity. Then if one of them says that the non-existent is a body in the state of non-existence and also a substance, it is said to him: The body is that which is composed, and the substance is that in which accidents subsist. Was composition subsisting in the body in pre-eternity, and accident in the substance? If he says yes, he has made an accident subsist in the non-existent, which is impossible. If he says no, he has posited a body without composition and a substance without accident subsisting in it, which invalidates the definition of body as composed and substance as bearer of accidents, and this validates the statement of the anthropomorphists and the Christians. And truthful is he who said: The Mu'tazila are the effeminate of the Dahriyya. And besides this, the Mu'tazila have corrupt principles by which they have themselves refuted the proof of the origination of the world. Likewise the Karramiyya and other people of innovation, except that we have omitted mentioning them for fear of prolixity, and we will indicate some of that when we come to the discussion with them in refuting their schools. The people of truth have many ways of proving the origination of the world; we have refrained from mentioning them to avoid prolixity and because we consider this method sufficient. And by understanding this summary, the falsehood of the statement of everyone who claims the eternity of anything other than God is known.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila position on how the world becomes originated (hadith). Nasafi begins by noting that an existent cannot be described with accidents like motion, rest, etc., in its first moment of existence, nor in non-existence. Then he addresses the Mu'tazila claim that events (ahdath) are not an attribute of God but identical to the originated thing. He poses a dilemma: the word 'ihdath' (bringing into existence) — is it an attribute of God, or the originated itself, or something else? If it is an attribute of God, the Mu'tazila have abandoned their school (since they deny attributes). If it is something other than God, is it eternal or originated? If eternal, they admit a second eternal. If originated, they fall into infinite regress (tasalsul) because each ihdath would need another ihdath. If they say it is the essence itself, then the world's essence was in non-existence as an ihdath, implying that in pre-eternity the world's essence (substances, accidents, bodies) was already present, making it eternal — contradicting its origination. Then Nasafi refutes their redefinition of 'originated' as 'coming to be in a state it was not in before'. He argues that this meaning either refers to the essence or is additional; both are shown to be impossible. He then shifts to another argument: existence and thingness are intrinsic, not by a meaning. He asks whether the non-existent was an essence (dhat). If they say no, then how could it be a thing? If yes, then it was not existent. Their position ultimately aligns with the Dahriyya (materialists) or is even worse. Nasafi then refutes the claim that the non-existent is a body or substance, showing that it would require composition or accidents in non-existence, which is absurd. He concludes by noting that the Mu'tazila have many other corrupt principles, and the people of truth have sufficient proofs for the origination of the world, so this summary suffices to refute all claims of eternal entities besides God.

Key Terms

ذات
محدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that defining 'originated' as 'change of state' solves the problem.
Correction: Nasafi shows that this redefinition still leads to absurdity because it either equates to the essence (making the world eternal) or introduces an additional attribute (which the Mu'tazila deny).

Checkpoint
What happens if the Mu'tazila say that the world's essence itself is ihdath?
A) The world becomes eternal.
B) The world is created in time.
C) God's attributes are affirmed.
D) Infinite regress occurs.

Key Takeaway
The third option leads to the world being eternal, and the redefinition of 'originated' is shown to be incoherent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the world's existence is not essential to it—it came from non-existence by Allah's will—then your own existence is a gift sustained every moment. Where in your daily life do you act as if your existence is self-sufficient, forgetting that you are contingent and that Allah upholds you at every instant? What concrete reminder will you set for today to keep this dependence alive in your heart?
?
The Mu'tazila tried to redefine 'originated' to escape the conclusion of the world's eternity, twisting clear truths. In what area of your faith or practice do you find yourself softening, reinterpreting, or rationalizing what you know to be true from the Qur'an and Sunnah to avoid discomfort or accountability? Will you sincerely repent from this evasion and ask Allah to grant you the courage to accept His words as they are?

Allah's Existence
advanced
8 min
Intrinsic Existence and the Dahriyya Comparison
Nasafi presents the intrinsic existence argument and compares Mu'tazila to Dahriyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila view on non-existent entities leads to absurdities similar to those of the Dahriyya (materialists) and even worse, and why their claim that non-existents are bodies or substances is impossible.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila end up affirming the pre-eternity of all world-parts, making them worse than the Dahriyya who only posited a prime matter.

Nasafi now attacks the Mu'tazila claim that non-existent things have essences or are bodies/substances. By showing that existence and thingness are intrinsic, he forces them into admitting that all things were present in pre-eternity. He then compares this to the positions of the Dahriyya and the hylé theorists, concluding that the Mu'tazila are even worse. This lesson covers the final set of arguments and the conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic from 'then it is said to them' to the end. Notice how Nasafi shifts to a new argument about existence and thingness being intrinsic.
2
Understand the intrinsic existence argument
Nasafi argues that existence and thingness are not added attributes. He asks whether the non-existent was an essence. If not, it cannot be a thing; if yes, it was not existent.
3
Compare to Dahriyya and hylé
Nasafi shows that the Mu'tazila position is even worse than the materialists because they posit all parts of the world in pre-eternity, while the Dahriyya only posited a prime matter.
4
Examine the body/substance claim
If non-existents are bodies or substances, they must have composition and accidents. Since these cannot subsist in non-existence, the definitions of body and substance are invalidated.
5
See the final verdict
Nasafi concludes by noting that this summary suffices to refute all who claim eternity for anything other than God.

Source Text

والجوهر والجسم، فأما الموجود فيستحيل اتصافه في أول أحوال وجوده بأنه متحرك أو ساكن أو ماش أو قاعد أو أكل أو شارب، فيستحيل أيضا اتصافه بها في حالة العدم، ثم من زعم منهم أن الأحداث ليس بصفة للباري عز وجل بل عين المحدث، فيقال : ما معنى قولكم بأن العالم محدث، أكان محدثا بأحداث هو صفة الله تعالى قائمة به أو بإحداث هو عين المحدث أو بإحداث هو غير المحدث وليس بصفة الله تعالى قائمة به ؟ فإن قالوا : حدث بإحداث هو صفة الله تعالى، قيل هذا ترك منكم مذهبكم وإن زعموا أنه حدث بإحداث هو غير الله تعالى، قيل أقديم هو أم محدث؟ فإن قالوا هو قديم فقد تركوا مذهبهم وإن قالوا هو محدث، قيل: إن حدث أيضا بإحداث آخر أم لا بإحداث؟ فإن قالوا: لا بإحداث فقد أحالوا وعطلوا الصانع حيث جوزوا حدوث حادث لا بإحداث، وإن قالوا حدث بإحداث آخر سئلوا عن الإحداث الثاني والثالث فيتسلسل إلى غير نهاية، وفيه تعليق حدوث العالم بما يستحيل ثبوته، وإن قالوا حدث بإحداث هو ذاته، فقد جعلوا ذات العالم في العدم إحداثا وهو في الأزل كان ذاتا وكان جوهرا وأعراض وأجساما فكانت محدثة في الأزل، والموجود في الأزل لن يكون محدثا بل يكون قديما ، فإذا كان العالم قديما موجودا في الأزل، فاعترضوا على هذا وزعموا أن معنى قولنا: إن العالم حدث أي حصل على حالة لم يكن عليها قبل هذه الحالة ، معنى راجع إلى ذات العالم أم هي معنى وراء ذات العالم فبأي الجواب أجابوا فقد أبطلنا، وتبين أنه حصل بهذا الاعتراض لاغيا هاذيا ثم يقال لهم إذا كان الموجود موجودا لذاته لا لمعنى، وكذا الشيء شيئا لذاته لا لمعنى، أكان المعدوم ذاتا؟ فإن قالوا: لا، قيل: لم كان شيئا والشيء شيء لذاته، وكذا العرض والجوهر، وإن قالوا: كان المعدوم ذاتا قيل لم يكن موجودا، والذات الذي لأجله يتصف بالوجود قائم بظهر بهذا أي قولهم نتيجة قول الدهرية بل هو عين ذلك بل هو شر من قول أصحاب الهيولى بدرجات فإن أولئك ما أثبتوا في الأزل إلا الهيولى وهو شيء متحد الذات عندهم لا كمية له ولا كيفية وليس بجوهر ولا عرض، وهؤلاء أثبتوا جميع أجزاء العالم في الأزل، ثم من قال منهم أن المعدوم جسم في حالة العدم وجوهر أيضا قيل له الجسم هو المتركب، والجوهر ما قام به الأعراض، أكان التركب قائما بالجسم في الأزل والعرض بالجوهر؟ فإن قال: نعم، فقد جعل العرض قائما بالمعدوم وهو محال، وإن قال: لا، فقد أثبت جسما لا تركيب له وجوهرا لم يقم به العرض، وفيه إبطال كون الجسم متركبا، والجوهر حاملا للأعراض، وفيه تصحيح قول المجسمة والنصارى، ولقد صدق من قال : إن المعتزلة مخانيث الدهرية، ووراء هذا للمعتزلة أصول فاسدة أبطلوا بها على أنفسهم إثبات حدوث العالم. وكذا الكرامية وغيرهم من أهل البدع، إلا أنا تركنا ذكرها مخافة التطويل ونشير إلى بعض ذلك إذا انتهينا إلى الكلام معهم في إبطال مذاهبهم، ولأهل الحق طرق كثيرة في إثبات حدوث العالم، أعرضنا عن ذكرها تحرزا عن التطويل وعلما منا بكافية هذه الطريقة. وبالوقوف على هذه الجملة عرف بطلان قول كل من يدعي قدم شيء ما سوى الله
And the substance and the body. As for the existent, it is impossible for it to be described in the first state of its existence as moving or stationary or walking or sitting or eating or drinking, and it is also impossible for it to be described with these in the state of non-existence. Then whoever among them claims that events [originations] are not an attribute of the Creator, glory be to Him, but are identical to the originated thing, it is said: What is the meaning of your statement that the world is originated? Was it originated by an originating (ihdath) that is an attribute of God, exalted, subsisting in Him, or by an originating that is identical to the originated, or by an originating that is other than the originated and not an attribute of God, exalted, subsisting in Him? If they say: It originated by an originating that is an attribute of God, it is said: This is an abandonment of your school. If they claim that it originated by an originating that is other than God, it is said: Is that originating eternal or originated? If they say it is eternal, they have abandoned their school; if they say it is originated, it is said: Did it also originate by another originating or not by an originating? If they say: Not by an originating, they have committed an absurdity and negated the Maker, for they allowed the occurrence of an originated event without an originating. If they say it originated by another originating, they are asked about the second and third originating, and so on ad infinitum, and in this is the suspension of the origination of the world upon something whose establishment is impossible. And if they say it originated by an originating that is its essence, then they have made the essence of the world in non-existence an originating, while in pre-eternity it was an essence and was substance, accidents, and bodies, so they were originated in pre-eternity. And that which exists in pre-eternity cannot be originated but is eternal. So if the world is eternal, existing in pre-eternity, then they object to this and claim that the meaning of our statement 'the world originated' is that it came to be in a state it was not in before this state. Is this meaning referable to the essence of the world or is it a meaning beyond the essence of the world? Whichever answer they give, we have refuted it. And it becomes clear that this objection is vain and absurd. Then it is said to them: If the existent exists by itself and not by a meaning, and likewise a thing is a thing by itself and not by a meaning, was the non-existent an essence? If they say no, it is said: Why was it a thing, while a thing is a thing by itself? Likewise the accident and the substance. And if they say the non-existent was an essence, it is said: Then it was not existent. And the essence by which it is described with existence subsists in...? By this their statement is the result of the statement of the Dahriyya, rather it is the same, rather it is worse than the statement of the proponents of hylé by degrees. For those only posited in pre-eternity the hylé, which is a thing unified in essence according to them, having no quantity nor quality, and is neither substance nor accident. And these [Mu'tazila] posited all parts of the world in pre-eternity. Then if one of them says that the non-existent is a body in the state of non-existence and also a substance, it is said to him: The body is that which is composed, and the substance is that in which accidents subsist. Was composition subsisting in the body in pre-eternity, and accident in the substance? If he says yes, he has made an accident subsist in the non-existent, which is impossible. If he says no, he has posited a body without composition and a substance without accident subsisting in it, which invalidates the definition of body as composed and substance as bearer of accidents, and this validates the statement of the anthropomorphists and the Christians. And truthful is he who said: The Mu'tazila are the effeminate of the Dahriyya. And besides this, the Mu'tazila have corrupt principles by which they have themselves refuted the proof of the origination of the world. Likewise the Karramiyya and other people of innovation, except that we have omitted mentioning them for fear of prolixity, and we will indicate some of that when we come to the discussion with them in refuting their schools. The people of truth have many ways of proving the origination of the world; we have refrained from mentioning them to avoid prolixity and because we consider this method sufficient. And by understanding this summary, the falsehood of the statement of everyone who claims the eternity of anything other than God is known.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila position on how the world becomes originated (hadith). Nasafi begins by noting that an existent cannot be described with accidents like motion, rest, etc., in its first moment of existence, nor in non-existence. Then he addresses the Mu'tazila claim that events (ahdath) are not an attribute of God but identical to the originated thing. He poses a dilemma: the word 'ihdath' (bringing into existence) — is it an attribute of God, or the originated itself, or something else? If it is an attribute of God, the Mu'tazila have abandoned their school (since they deny attributes). If it is something other than God, is it eternal or originated? If eternal, they admit a second eternal. If originated, they fall into infinite regress (tasalsul) because each ihdath would need another ihdath. If they say it is the essence itself, then the world's essence was in non-existence as an ihdath, implying that in pre-eternity the world's essence (substances, accidents, bodies) was already present, making it eternal — contradicting its origination. Then Nasafi refutes their redefinition of 'originated' as 'coming to be in a state it was not in before'. He argues that this meaning either refers to the essence or is additional; both are shown to be impossible. He then shifts to another argument: existence and thingness are intrinsic, not by a meaning. He asks whether the non-existent was an essence (dhat). If they say no, then how could it be a thing? If yes, then it was not existent. Their position ultimately aligns with the Dahriyya (materialists) or is even worse. Nasafi then refutes the claim that the non-existent is a body or substance, showing that it would require composition or accidents in non-existence, which is absurd. He concludes by noting that the Mu'tazila have many other corrupt principles, and the people of truth have sufficient proofs for the origination of the world, so this summary suffices to refute all claims of eternal entities besides God.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Mu'tazila position is more rational than materialists.
Correction: Nasafi argues the opposite: they are worse because they posit all specific entities as pre-eternal, while materialists only posit a featureless prime matter.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, how do the Mu'tazila compare to the Dahriyya?
A) They are better because they believe in God.
B) They are the same.
C) They are worse because they posit all world-parts in pre-eternity.
D) They are unrelated.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila position on non-existents leads to absurdities that make them even worse than materialists.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazila ended up worse than atheists by over-intellectualizing the faith. Where in your own heart do you rely on your reasoning more than the clear texts of revelation, and what is the consequence for your certainty?
?
Nasafi calls the Mu'tazila 'the effeminate of the Dahriyya'—a harsh reminder that compromising on tawhid leads to absurdity. In what subtle ways do you allow modern materialistic assumptions to shape your understanding of Allah's exclusive eternity?
?
The proof in this passage is said to be sufficient to refute anyone who claims eternity for anything other than God. After reading these arguments, do you truly live as if nothing—no person, no career, no possession—deserves the status of 'eternal' in your heart? If not, what would it take to uproot that?

Allah's Existence
beginner

The World's Contingency Necessitates a Creator
Nasafi enumerates the argument from contingency and particularization for a creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses the contingency of the world and the need for a specificator to prove the existence of a creator.

Core Idea
Contingent beings need a specificator to bring them from non-existence to existence.

Nasafi has already proven that the world is originated (muhdath). Now he argues that an originated being cannot be necessary in existence (wajib) but must be contingent (ja'iz). Since it admits both existence and non-existence, it cannot transition from non-existence to existence without a specificator (mukhassis). He uses analogies from everyday experience to demonstrate this rational necessity.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the initial premise
The world is originated, so it cannot be necessary in existence (eternal). It must be contingent—capable of existing or not existing.
Nasafi assumes the world's origination has been proven earlier.
2
Understand the need for a specificator
Anything that can be in two states cannot choose one without a cause that specifies it. This cause is called a specificator (mukhassis).
The body analogy illustrates this: motion or rest requires a cause.
3
Examine the non-existence argument
Non-existence is the natural state of a contingent thing, so existence requires a cause that overrides this default.
Non-existence does not need a cause; existence does.
4
Consider the argument from possible variations
The world could have been different in size, quality, etc. Its actual specific form therefore needs a specificator.
5
Reflect on the building analogy
Just as a building obviously has a builder, the world's existence and order point to a creator. Denying this is ignorance.
This ties the rational proof to common experience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تبصرة الأدلة لأبي المعين النسفي ج الفصل الثالث ۲۲۳
۱ - الكلام في أن العالم له محدث:
وإذ أثبتنا بالدليل أن العالم محدث، فإن المحدث جائز الوجود لا واجب الوجود، إذ لو كان واجب الوجود لكان مستحيل العدم وكان قديما وقد ثبت حدوثه، وإنه قبل الحدوث كان معدوما، دل أنه ليس بمستحيل العدم، ولا بواجب الوجود بل كان جائز الوجود وجائز العدم، وما يجوز عليه الحالان، لا يختص بأحدهما إلا بتخصيص مخصص، كالجسم لما جاز أن يكون متحركا، وإن يكون ساكنا، لم يختص بإحدى الحالتين إلا بمعنى يوجب اختصاصه بها وهو الحركة أو السكون فكذا هذا، بل كان العدم أولى به من الوجود لولا معنى بدلت به الحالة؛ لأنه كان عدماً في العدم، وبدلت الحالة بالوجود فلابد من وجود معنى أوجب تبدله ولأن العدم نفي فلا يقتضي تعليلا ولا مخصصا بخلاف الوجود، واعتبر بعدم البناء ووجوده، في مكان مخصوص ولأن العالم يتصور أن يكون على غير هذه الهيئة والقدر ويتوهم أن يكون أكبر وأزين من هذا، ويتصور أن يكون أدون من هذا فكانت هذه الحالة مع ما يخالفانه في الجودة ( ) والرداءة والصغر والكبر في حيز الإمكان فاختصاصه بهذه الحالة لا يكون إلا بتخصيص مخصص، وبهذه الدلالة يستدل على وجود الباني لكل بناء يشاهد في الدنيا، وتقررت هذه الدلالة في العقول، حتى إن من أجاز وجود ذلك جزافا من غير صانع له عد متجاهلا في نفسه.
Tabsirat al-Adilla by Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi, part. Chapter Three. 1 - Discussion that the world has a creator: And since we have proven by evidence that the world is originated, then the originated is contingent in existence, not necessary in existence. For if it were necessary in existence, it would be impossible of non-existence and would be eternal, and its origination has been established. And that before origination it was non-existent indicates that it is not impossible of non-existence, nor is it necessary in existence, but rather it was contingent in existence and contingent in non-existence. And that which admits both states is not particularized with one of them except by the particularization of a particularizer. Like the body: when it admits being moving and being stationary, it is not particularized with one of the two states except by a meaning that necessitates its particularization with it, namely motion or rest. So likewise this. Rather, non-existence was more fitting to it than existence were it not for a meaning that changed the state; because it was non-existence in non-existence, and the state was changed to existence, so there must be a meaning that necessitates its change. And because non-existence is a negation, it does not require a cause nor a particularizer, unlike existence. And consider by the non-existence of a building and its existence in a specific place. And because the world can be conceived to be other than this form and measure, and can be imagined to be greater and more beautiful than this, and can be conceived to be lesser than this; so this state, along with what differs from it in quality and defectiveness and smallness and bigness, is in the realm of possibility. So its particularization with this state is only by the particularization of a particularizer. And by this indication one infers the existence of the builder for every building observed in the world. And this indication has been established in minds, such that whoever permits the existence of that haphazardly without a maker for it is considered ignorant in himself.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the existence of a creator (muhdith) for the world, relying on the argument from contingency and particularization. The author begins by recalling that the world has been proven to be originated (muhdath). He then argues that an originated being must be contingent (ja'iz al-wujud), not necessary (wajib al-wujud), because if it were necessary, it would be eternal and impossible to be non-existent, but its origination (hadath) shows it was non-existent before, so it cannot be necessary. Thus it is contingent, meaning it can exist or not exist. Something that admits both states cannot be in one state without a specificator (mukhassis). The author provides an analogy: a body can be either moving or at rest, and it is only in one of these states due to a cause (motion or rest). Similarly, the world was non-existent and then existed, so there must be a cause that changed its state. He emphasizes that non-existence does not require a cause, but existence does. Furthermore, the world could have been different in form, size, quality, etc., so its specific configuration requires a specificator. This is the same reasoning used to infer a builder for any building. The proof is so clear that anyone who denies it is considered ignorant.

Key Terms
العالم
محدث
واجب الوجود
جائز الوجود
مخصص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The world could have come into existence randomly without a cause.
Correction: Nasafi argues that contingency requires a specificator; random existence is irrational and equivalent to ignorance.

Checkpoint
Why does Nasafi say that the world cannot be necessary in existence (wajib al-wujud)?
A) Because it is composed of parts
B) Because it has been proven to be originated and was non-existent before
C) Because it is changing
D) Because it has a creator

Key Takeaway
The world's existence and specific configuration cannot be random; they necessarily point to a creator who particularizes it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the universe, do you truly recognise that its very existence is not self-sufficient? How does this realisation change the way you see your own life—does it make you more aware of your dependence on Allah every single moment?
?
The passage says non-existence was more fitting for the world before it existed. Reflect on the fact that you could have easily not existed. Does this truth humble you? How does it affect your gratitude to the One who brought you into existence?
?
If the specific configuration of this world points to a specificator, then what about the specific details of your life—your circumstances, abilities, and trials? Are you living as if they are random, or do you see them as intentionally particularized by Allah? What would change if you truly believed that?

Impossibility of Self-Creation After Existing
Al-Nasafi presents two arguments against self-creation after existing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why self-creation after existing is logically impossible according to Al-Nasafi's two arguments.

Core Idea
Self-creation after existing requires either uncaused existence or creating what already exists.

Al-Nasafi begins by dismissing the notion that something could create itself after it already exists. He presents two logical reasons why this is impossible. Let's examine his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully.
Read the passage once to get the flow, then focus on the two reasons mentioned.
Notice the structure: 'من وجهين' introduces the two reasons.
2
Identify the two aspects of impossibility.
The first reason involves existence without a creator; the second involves bringing an existent into existence.
3
Reflect on the logical problems.
Think about why each reason is problematic: uncaused existence contradicts causality, and double creation is nonsense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يتوهم أنه أحدث نفسه بنفسه، لأنه إن أحدث نفسه بعدما صار موجودا فهو محال من وجهين: أحدهما وجوده قبل إحداث نفسه لا بإحداث محدث وتخصيص مخصص إياه بالحدوث وهو باطل، والآخر إيجاده نفسه بعدما صار موجودا وإيجاد الموجود مستحيل. ولا يتوهم أيضا أنه أحدث نفسه في حالة العدم، لما أن وجود الفعل من المعدوم محال.
Let it not be imagined that it brought itself into existence, because if it brought itself into existence after having become existent, it is impossible from two aspects: one is its existence before bringing itself into existence without the bringing into existence of a bringer and the specification of a specifier of it with temporality, and that is false; and the other is its bringing itself into existence after it has become existent, and bringing an existent into existence is impossible. And let it also not be imagined that it brought itself into existence in the state of non-existence, because the existence of an act from the non-existent is impossible.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of any claim that the world or any being could have created itself. Al-Nasafi presents two arguments. First, if something were to create itself after it already exists, this involves a contradiction: it would have to exist before bringing itself into existence (to perform the act of creation), and also bringing an already existent thing into existence is nonsensical. Second, if it were to create itself while non-existent, this is impossible because a non-existent thing cannot perform any act. Thus, self-creation is logically impossible in both scenarios.

Key Terms
إحداث
محدث
مخصص
وجود
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A thing could cause its own existence after it exists, like a self-sustaining loop.
Correction: The passage shows this would require the thing to exist without a cause before its own act, which is logically contradictory.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is self-creation after existing impossible? (Choose the best answer)
A) Because the thing would not yet exist to perform the act
B) Because it involves either existence without a cause or bringing an existent into existence
C) Because everything must be created by God
D) Because it would require infinite regress

Key Takeaway
Self-creation after existing is impossible because it requires prior uncaused existence and cannot generate an already existent thing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever live as if you created yourself or own your existence, forgetting that every moment of your being depends on a Creator? What would change if you truly internalized that you cannot sustain yourself even for a second?
?
The passage says bringing an existent into existence is impossible. How does this refute the idea that you can 'renew' your own faith or existence without God's help? In what areas of your life are you acting as if you are self-sufficient?
?
Reflect on a time you felt you could 'self-create' your own purpose or destiny. How does this logical argument expose the fallacy of that feeling? What step will you take today to acknowledge your absolute dependence on Allah?

Impossibility of Self-Creation from Non-Existence
Al-Nasafi argues that self-creation in the state of non-existence is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why self-creation while non-existent is impossible according to Al-Nasafi.

Core Idea
A non-existent thing cannot perform any act, so self-creation from non-existence is impossible.

Al-Nasafi also refutes the idea that something could create itself while in a state of non-existence. This might seem to avoid the prior existence problem, but it is equally impossible because an act requires an agent.

Guided Path
1
Read the short Arabic passage.
Read the passage carefully. It is a single sentence that states the impossibility.
2
Understand the key principle.
The core principle is that no act can proceed from a non-existent entity.
Think about why: an act requires an existing agent.
3
Connect to the broader argument.
Recognize that this completes the refutation: self-creation is impossible in both scenarios.

And let it also not be imagined that it brought itself into existence in the state of non-existence, because the existence of an act from the non-existent is impossible.

First, if something were to create itself after it already exists, this involves a contradiction: it would have to exist before bringing itself into existence (to perform the act of creation), and also bringing an already existent thing into existence is nonsensical. Second, if it were to create itself while non-existent, this is impossible because a non-existent thing cannot perform any act. Thus, self-creation is logically impossible in both scenarios.

Proof from Human Limitation
Al-Nasafi proves the need for a Creator from human limitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses the contrast between human power over animals and inability to change one's own qualities to argue for an external Creator.

Core Idea
If you cannot change one hair, how can the world create itself?

Al-Nasafi begins by reminding us of the remarkable abilities humans have—taming animals, extracting resources from sea and air. Then he points to a stark limitation: we cannot alter our own physical features. This contrast sets up a powerful argument that the origin of the entire world from nothing is even more improbable.

Guided Path
1
Read the human abilities description
Read from the beginning of the passage to where Al-Nasafi describes human power over animals. Notice the tone of awe.
This sets the stage for the limitation to follow.
2
Identify the limitation
Find the part where Al-Nasafi says humans are incapable of changing a blameworthy quality like ugliness to beauty.
He gives specific examples: ugliness/beauty, short/tall, black/white.
3
Understand the logical move
Notice how Al-Nasafi moves from human inability to the impossibility of the world creating itself. He says 'even more unattainable'.
The argument is a fortiori: if you can't do a small thing, how can you do a big thing?
4
Connect to the conclusion
The conclusion is that the world must have a Creator. The passage doesn't state it explicitly here but leads to it.
The next argument will further support this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه: أن الآدمي مع أنه ليس بعرض بل هو جوهر، وليس بجماد بل هو نام، وليس بنبات بل هو حيوان وليس بعجم بل هو ناطق. وهذه الحالة النهاية في القوة والتدبير للحيوانات الأرضية، ولهذا يغلب بحيلة اللطيفة وتدابيره الصائبة جميع الحيوانات الأرضية، فيستسخر الفيلة العظام، والأسود الضارية، والحيات الناهشة فيستعملها في حوائجه كيف شاء وأراد، ويستخرج ما في قعور البحار من الحيوانات المائية، ويستنزل من الهواء والطيور الهوائية، ثم هو في حال كمال عقله وعلمه بالأمور، وتمام قوته وبصارته بوجوده الحيل والتدابير يعجز عن تغيير صفة له ذميمة إلى ما يستحليه ويهواه من مضاد تلك الصفة، كالدمامة والحسن، وقصر القامة وطولها، وسواد بشرته وبياضها، فلأن لا يتأتى ولا يتصور إيجاد أصل العالم مما هو معدوم أولى. يحققه أن كل عين من أعيان العالم اجتمعت فيه الطبائع المتضادة التي من شأنها التباين ومن طبعها التنافر، ولو تركت وطباعها لتباينت وتنافرت فدل وجودها على خلاف ما يقتضي شأنها أن ذلك ليس من قبل ذواتها بل بقادر لا يغالب وعزيز لا يمانع. وكذا اختلاف المتجانسات في الوقت، وتباين المتماثلات واجتماع المختلفات في الجوهر يقتضي مقدما قدم ومؤخرا آخر وجامعا جمع ومفرقا فرق إذ لو كان الأمر على مقتضى ذات كل منها ما اختلفت المتجانسات في الوقت ولا تباينت المتماثلات بالمحل لاستواء كل من ذلك فيما تقتضيه الذات، ولو اجتمعت المختلفات في الجوهر لتفرق ما يقتضيه ذات كل واحد منهما، وحيث كان الأمر على هذا، ووجد اختلاف فيما يوجب الذوات المستوية واستواء فيما يوجب الذوات المتفرقة كان ذلك دليلا على وجود صانع لها كامل القدرة نافذ المشيئة يفعل ما يشاء على حسب ما تقتضيه حكمته البالغة ومشيئته النافذة، وبالله التوفيق.
He verifies it: that the human being, although he is not an accident but a substance, and not inanimate but growing, and not a plant but an animal, and not non-rational but rational — and this is the ultimate state in strength and management for terrestrial animals; therefore he overcomes, with his subtle tricks and correct plans, all terrestrial animals, and subdues huge elephants, ferocious lions, and venomous snakes, employing them in his needs as he wishes, and extracts from the depths of the seas aquatic animals, and brings down from the air birds of the air. Then he, in a state of complete intellect and knowledge of things, and full strength and insight in devising tricks and plans, is incapable of changing a blameworthy quality of his to what he desires and craves from the opposite of that quality, such as ugliness and beauty, shortness of stature and tallness, blackness of his skin and whiteness — so that the bringing into existence of the origin of the world from what is non-existent is even more unattainable and unimaginable. He verifies it: that every individual entity of the entities of the world has in it the opposing natures which are characterized by distinction and by nature are averse; and if they were left to their natures, they would separate and become averse. So their existence contrary to what their nature requires indicates that this is not from themselves but from a powerful one who is not overcome, and a mighty one who is not resisted. Likewise, the difference of homogeneous things in time, and the distinction of similar things, and the coming together of different things in substance necessitate a bringer who brought, a delayer who delayed, a gatherer who gathered, and a separator who separated. For if the matter were according to the nature of each of them, homogeneous things would not differ in time, nor would similar things be distinct in location, because each of them would be equal in what the nature requires; and if different things in substance came together, they would separate according to what the nature of each one requires. And since the matter is this, and there is found difference in what requires uniform natures, and uniformity in what requires separate natures, that is evidence for the existence of a Maker for them, perfect in power, effective in will, who does what He wills according to what His profound wisdom and effective will require. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the existence of a necessary Creator through two arguments. First, Al-Nasafi uses the example of a human being: despite possessing intellect, power, and ability to tame animals and extract resources, a human is utterly incapable of changing even one of his own physical qualities (e.g., ugliness to beauty, short to tall). If a human cannot alter a single attribute of himself, then it is even more impossible for the entire world to come into existence from nothing by itself. Second, he argues from the composition of the world: every entity contains opposing natures (like heat and cold) that would naturally repel each other. Their coexistence in a stable form shows they are not self-caused but are held together by a powerful agent. Furthermore, the fact that homogeneous things differ in time and place, and dissimilar things coexist, points to a creator who brings together and separates according to His will. The conclusion is that there must be a Maker who is perfectly powerful and whose will is effective, acting according to His wisdom.

جوهر
عرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the example of a human being's inability to change his own qualities demonstrate?
A) That humans are weak and helpless.
B) That if humans cannot change a single quality, then the world's origin from nothing is even more impossible.
C) That humans should be grateful for their qualities.
D) That only God can change human qualities.

Key Takeaway
Human inability to change one's own attributes shows that the world's existence from nothing requires an external Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You can command elephants and extract pearls from the ocean, but you cannot make yourself taller or change the color of your skin. What does that tell you about your true power? And if you cannot alter even one hair, how can you claim to be the master of your own destiny? Are you living with the humility that your existence depends entirely on Another, or are you acting as if you are self-sufficient? What will you do today to remind yourself of your limits?
?
This lesson proves that the existence of the world requires a Creator because a small change is beyond you. But do you actually feel this dependency every moment? When you look in the mirror and dislike what you see, do you recognize your limitation and turn to the One who can change hearts and forms, or do you despair or obsess over things beyond your control? How can you train yourself to see your helplessness as a doorway to faith?
?
If bringing the world into existence from nothing is even more impossible than you changing your skin color, what does that imply about your efforts to control outcomes in your life—your career, your relationships, your future? Where in your life are you most resisting the fact that you are not in control? What would it look like to surrender that area to the Creator today, trusting that He alone can bring good from nothing?

Proof from Opposing Natures in the World
Al-Nasafi proves a Maker from the composition of opposing natures and patterns in the world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the coexistence of opposing natures in entities and the patterns of homogeneity and difference point to a powerful Maker.

Core Idea
Opposites don't hold themselves together; something greater must.

Al-Nasafi now turns to the physical composition of the world itself. Each entity contains elements that naturally repel each other. Their stable existence cannot be self-caused; it demands a powerful agent. Moreover, patterns of similarity and difference in time and place reinforce this conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument from opposing natures
Read the first part of the passage describing how every entity contains opposing natures that would naturally separate.
Note the terms: طبائع متضادة (opposing natures).
2
Understand the logical inference
If left to themselves, these natures would separate. Their continued union indicates an external holder.
The text says 'فدل وجودها على خلاف ما يقتضي شأنها أن ذلك ليس من قبل ذواتها بل بقادر لا يغالب'.
3
Read the second observation
Read the part about homogeneous things differing in time, similar things being distinct, and different things coming together.
This is a separate but complementary observation.
4
Connect both observations to the conclusion
Both observations lead to the same conclusion: there must be a Maker who is perfectly powerful and wise.
The final sentence summarizes: 'كان ذلك دليلا على وجود صانع لها كامل القدرة نافذ المشيئة'.

يحققه: أن الآدمي مع أنه ليس بعرض بل هو جوهر، وليس بجماد بل هو نام، وليس بنبات بل هو حيوان وليس بعجم بل هو ناطق. وهذه الحالة النهاية في القوة والتدبير للحيوانات الأرضية، ولهذا يغلب بحيلة اللطيفة وتدابيره الصائبة جميع الحيوانات الأرضية، فيستسخر الفيلة العظام، والأسود الضارية، والحيات الناهشة فيستعملها في حوائجه كيف شاء وأراد، ويستخرج ما في قعور البحار من الحيوانات المائية، ويستنزل من الهواء والطيور الهوائية، ثم هو في حال كمال عقله وعلمه بالأمور، وتمام قوته وبصارته بوجوده الحيل والتدابير يعجز عن تغيير صفة له ذميمة إلى ما يستحليه ويهواه من مضاد تلك الصفة، كالدمامة والحسن، وقصر القامة وطولها، وسواد بشرته وبياضها، فلأن لا يتأتى ولا يتصور إيجاد أصل العالم مما هو معدوم أولى. يحققه أن كل عين من أعيان العالم اجتمعت فيه الطبائع المتضادة التي من شأنها التباين ومن طبعها التنافر، ولو تركت وطباعها لتباينت وتنافرت فدل وجودها على خلاف ما يقتضي شأنها أن ذلك ليس من قبل ذواتها بل بقادر لا يغالب وعزيز لا يمانع. وكذا اختلاف المتجانسات في الوقت، وتباين المتماثلات واجتماع المختلفات في الجوهر يقتضي مقدما قدم ومؤخرا آخر وجامعا جمع ومفرقا فرق إذ لو كان الأمر على مقتضى ذات كل منها ما اختلفت المتجانسات في الوقت ولا تباينت المتماثلات بالمحل لاستواء كل من ذلك فيما تقتضيه الذات، ولو اجتمعت المختلفات في الجوهر لتفرق ما يقتضيه ذات كل واحد منهما، وحيث كان الأمر على هذا، ووجد اختلاف فيما يوجب الذوات المستوية واستواء فيما يوجب الذوات المتفرقة كان ذلك دليلا على وجود صانع لها كامل القدرة نافذ المشيئة يفعل ما يشاء على حسب ما تقتضيه حكمته البالغة ومشيئته النافذة، وبالله التوفيق.
He verifies it: that the human being, although he is not an accident but a substance, and not inanimate but growing, and not a plant but an animal, and not non-rational but rational — and this is the ultimate state in strength and management for terrestrial animals; therefore he overcomes, with his subtle tricks and correct plans, all terrestrial animals, and subdues huge elephants, ferocious lions, and venomous snakes, employing them in his needs as he wishes, and extracts from the depths of the seas aquatic animals, and brings down from the air birds of the air. Then he, in a state of complete intellect and knowledge of things, and full strength and insight in devising tricks and plans, is incapable of changing a blameworthy quality of his to what he desires and craves from the opposite of that quality, such as ugliness and beauty, shortness of stature and tallness, blackness of his skin and whiteness — so that the bringing into existence of the origin of the world from what is non-existent is even more unattainable and unimaginable. He verifies it: that every individual entity of the entities of the world has in it the opposing natures which are characterized by distinction and by nature are averse; and if they were left to their natures, they would separate and become averse. So their existence contrary to what their nature requires indicates that this is not from themselves but from a powerful one who is not overcome, and a mighty one who is not resisted. Likewise, the difference of homogeneous things in time, and the distinction of similar things, and the coming together of different things in substance necessitate a bringer who brought, a delayer who delayed, a gatherer who gathered, and a separator who separated. For if the matter were according to the nature of each of them, homogeneous things would not differ in time, nor would similar things be distinct in location, because each of them would be equal in what the nature requires; and if different things in substance came together, they would separate according to what the nature of each one requires. And since the matter is this, and there is found difference in what requires uniform natures, and uniformity in what requires separate natures, that is evidence for the existence of a Maker for them, perfect in power, effective in will, who does what He wills according to what His profound wisdom and effective will require. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the existence of a necessary Creator through two arguments. First, Al-Nasafi uses the example of a human being: despite possessing intellect, power, and ability to tame animals and extract resources, a human is utterly incapable of changing even one of his own physical qualities (e.g., ugliness to beauty, short to tall). If a human cannot alter a single attribute of himself, then it is even more impossible for the entire world to come into existence from nothing by itself. Second, he argues from the composition of the world: every entity contains opposing natures (like heat and cold) that would naturally repel each other. Their coexistence in a stable form shows they are not self-caused but are held together by a powerful agent. Furthermore, the fact that homogeneous things differ in time and place, and dissimilar things coexist, points to a creator who brings together and separates according to His will. The conclusion is that there must be a Maker who is perfectly powerful and whose will is effective, acting according to His wisdom.

Misconception: Some think the argument is merely about complexity or design, but it specifically uses the coexistence of contrary elements and patterns that violate natural tendencies.
Correction: Al-Nasafi's argument is not just that the world is complex, but that it contains elements that naturally repel, yet they are held together—this requires an external powerful agent.

Checkpoint
What does the coexistence of opposing natures in a single entity indicate?
A) That natures can change and become compatible.
B) That there is a powerful external agent holding them together.
C) That entities are self-sufficient and need no cause.
D) That opposing natures do not really exist.

Key Takeaway
The stable coexistence of opposing natures and the patterns of difference and similarity in the world prove the existence of a perfectly powerful and wise Maker.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own body—where heat, cold, wetness, and dryness coexist in delicate balance—do you truly pause to recognize the One who holds them together? How often do you take this stability for granted? Commit today to uttering 'Allahu Akbar' whenever you notice your breath or heartbeat, acknowledging the Power that sustains them.
?
You observe patterns every day: similar things in different places, opposite things united, yet you rarely stop to ask, 'Why is this not chaos?' This passage tells you the answer is not in the things themselves but in a wise Maker. When you ignore this sign, what does that say about your awareness of Him? Will you let today's reading change how you see the world—as a constant testimony to His will?
?
The argument ends with a Maker who 'does what He wills according to profound wisdom.' Do you truly believe that every event in your life—even the painful ones—is governed by that same perfect wisdom? If so, where is your trust? If not, what would it take for you to surrender fully? Write one area of your life where you resist His will, and ask Him to grant you submission.
